## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed single document verifier stands where the bundle prescribes boundary-matched verification, SKILL.md's step four names cargo test, doctests, compile-fail tests, property or fuzz tests, clippy -D warnings, and any concurrency verification the code deserves, chosen per touched boundary rather than run as a fixed battery
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because section 4 assigns each gate its jurisdiction, doctests for API contracts, compile-fail for misuse contracts, property tests for invariants, fuzzing for untrusted-input frontiers, loom for interleavings, so the gate mix is a function of what boundary changed
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one-size gate batteries fail in both directions, running loom on everything wastes verification budget, while cargo test alone on concurrency code is exactly the passed-once superstition RC2-24 warns proves almost nothing
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: code verification gates for this theme's work, the seed's document verifier keeps its own corpus jurisdiction
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to adopt the boundary-to-gate mapping as the review contract, each change names its touched boundaries and shows the matched gates green
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the gates form a severity ladder mirroring the decision ladder's verification rung, from clippy always on, through contract gates when APIs change, to loom and Miri reserved for the concurrency and unsafe frontiers, so gate escalation is itself a signal of what kind of code the change is

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed four generic bullets stand where the mapped file contains an explicit LLM operating manual, section 11's seven-rung decision ladder, classify the code, then choose ownership, error, concurrency, API-stability, and verification surfaces in order, with unsafe minimization as the final rung
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the ladder exists because the file's own warning is that an LLM should not treat this as a buffet, sixty patterns invite arbitrary sampling, and the ladder converts them into forced sequential choices each with a bounded option set
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: buffet usage produces locally impressive, globally incoherent code, a GAT-heavy trait beside a stringly-typed error surface, the exact mismatch the ladder's ordered surfaces prevent
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: agent behavior over this theme's material, generic dispatch lives with the routing theme and delivery-process agent rules with rust-coder-01's territory
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace the generic bullets with the seven rungs verbatim-close, plus the skeptical question from SKILL.md step three as the standing cross-check at every rung
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the ladder's rungs are ordered by irreversibility, code classification and ownership shape everything downstream while verification mix can be revised late, so the ladder front-loads the decisions that are costliest to change, a structure worth copying into any agent prompt built from this theme

## Section 018: Workload Model

- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed's symbol-count boundary misses how this theme's effort actually distributes, per-boundary cost rather than per-symbol cost, a change touching one well-typed module is cheap at any size while a change crossing API, error, and concurrency surfaces at once carries three rungs of decisions and three gate escalations
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the ladder prices work by surfaces crossed, each crossed surface adds a decision, its clauses, its ledger entry, and its matched gates, so two small diffs can differ tenfold in reliability workload

## Section 019: Reliability Target

- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each target restates a top-tier pattern as an invariant, the anti-pattern target operationalizes the rejection list, the typed-error target holds RC2-12's ninety-seven-point line, and the unsafe target is RC2-53's own definition of the pattern

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed's corpus-process bullets stand beside the file's own retry-adjacent doctrine, cancellation and backpressure as first-class design surfaces, bounded channels making throughput limits visible, cancellation tokens making shutdown cooperative, and cancel-safe select discipline preventing retried futures from corrupting half-consumed state
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because RC2-21's stated logic is that unbounded queues hide problems until memory pressure becomes the symptom, so backpressure is not throttling etiquette but failure-visibility engineering, the bounded channel converts overload from a delayed crash into an immediate, attributable signal
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: retry logic wrapped around cancel-unsafe futures is the compounding trap, each retry of a future that owned half-read state re-enters corrupted ground, RC2-22's ownership discipline exists so that retrying is safe by construction rather than by luck
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: retry and backpressure doctrine for code under this theme, corpus-process retry rules keep the seed's jurisdiction, and HTTP-level retry policy lives with the backend themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the code-level regime, bound every high-throughput channel, token every long-lived task, keep select branches cancel-safe, and make retry decisions only at boundaries where state ownership is provably clean
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the doctrine links backpressure to diagnosability, a bounded channel's fullness is a measurable saturation signal while an unbounded one's growth is silent until terminal, so the bounded choice simultaneously prevents the failure and creates the observability the failure would need, one decision buying both

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed's generic records stand beside the file's own observability doctrine, RC2-38's structured tracing with spans, fields, and correlation IDs because async systems become opaque fast, RC2-39's secrecy wrappers because leaks are rarely caught by type-checking alone, and RC2-15's actionable diagnostics with exact locations and repair hints
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the three patterns share one premise, failures must be reconstructable after the fact, spans reconstruct control flow across tasks, typed secrets keep reconstruction artifacts safe to share, and located diagnostics make the reconstruction's endpoint actionable
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the anti-pattern is named in RC2-38's avoid-when, dumping whole payloads without filtering, logs that are simultaneously an observability failure and a secret-handling failure, the two patterns violated by one lazy line
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: what code under this theme must record, corpus-audit records keep the seed's jurisdiction, and pipeline-level telemetry lives with ops themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the code-level floor, spans with correlation fields on every async workflow, secrecy types on every credential, and located, hint-bearing diagnostics on every user-facing parse or config failure
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the diagnostics pattern doubles as an observability pattern, RC2-15's exact-location-plus-repair-hint rule means each error message is a pre-written incident note, so investment in diagnostic quality is investment in incident speed, the same text serving the user and the responder
